Title: Timeline of quantum computing and communication

URL Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication

Published Time: 2003-03-05T00:30:43Z

Markdown Content:
From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

This [incomplete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists "Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists") list is frequently updated to include new information.

![Image 1](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png)The **inclusion of certain items in this list is [disputed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute "Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute")**. Please see the relevant discussion on the [talk page](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#Misleading_short_descriptions "Talk:Timeline of quantum computing and communication"). _(December 2024)_

This is a **timeline of [quantum computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computing "Quantum computing") and [communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication "Communication")**.

[Stephen Wiesner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Wiesner "Stephen Wiesner") invents [conjugate coding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjugate_coding "Conjugate coding").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-1)[[a]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-6)

13 June – [James L. Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_L._Park "James L. Park") ([Washington State University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_State_University "Washington State University"), [Pullman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pullman,_Washington "Pullman, Washington"))'s paper is received by _[Foundations of Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foundations\_of\_Physics "Foundations of Physics")_,[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-park-7) in which he describes the non possibility of disturbance in a quantum [transition state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_electron_transition "Atomic electron transition") in the context of a disproof of [quantum jumps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_jumps "Quantum jumps") in the concept of the atom described by [Bohr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niels_Bohr "Niels Bohr").[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Park-8)[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Bertlmann&Friis-9)[[b]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-18)

*   [Alexander Holevo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Holevo "Alexander Holevo")'s paper[[c]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-20) is published.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-21) The [Holevo bound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holevo_bound "Holevo bound") describes a limit of the quantity of classical information which is possible to quanta encode.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-22)
*   [Charles H. Bennett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_H._Bennett_(physicist) "Charles H. Bennett (physicist)") shows that computation can be done [reversibly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reversible_computing "Reversible computing").[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-23)

*   R. P. Poplavskii publishes "Thermodynamical models of information processing" (in Russian)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Poplavskii-24) which shows the computational infeasibility of simulating quantum systems on classical computers, due to the [superposition principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superposition_principle "Superposition principle").
*   [Roman Stanisław Ingarden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Stanis%C5%82aw_Ingarden "Roman Stanisław Ingarden"), a Polish mathematical physicist, submits the paper "Quantum Information Theory" in [Reports on Mathematical Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reports_on_Mathematical_Physics "Reports on Mathematical Physics"), vol. 10, pp.43–72, published 1976. It is one of the first attempts at creating a [quantum information theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information_theory "Quantum information theory"), showing that [Shannon information theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shannon_information_theory "Shannon information theory") cannot directly be generalized to the [quantum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_physics "Quantum physics") case, but rather that it is possible to construct a quantum information theory, which is a generalization of Shannon's theory, within the formalism of a generalized quantum mechanics of open systems and a generalized concept of observables (the so-called semi-observables).

*   [Paul Benioff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Benioff "Paul Benioff") describes the first quantum mechanical model of a computer. In this work, Benioff showed that a computer could operate under the laws of [quantum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics "Quantum mechanics") by describing a [Schrödinger equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation "Schrödinger equation") description of [Turing machines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_machine "Turing machine"), laying a foundation for further work in quantum computing. The paper[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-25) was submitted in June 1979 and published in April 1980.
*   [Yuri Manin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Manin "Yuri Manin") briefly motivates the idea of quantum computing.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-manin1980vychislimoe-26)
*   [Tommaso Toffoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tommaso_Toffoli "Tommaso Toffoli") introduces the reversible [Toffoli gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toffoli_gate "Toffoli gate"),[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-27) which (together with initialized [ancilla bits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancilla_bit "Ancilla bit")) is [functionally complete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_completeness "Functional completeness") for [reversible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reversible_computing "Reversible computing") classical computation.

At the first Conference on the Physics of Computation, held at the [Massachusetts Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology "Massachusetts Institute of Technology") (MIT) in May,[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-28) Paul Benioff and [Richard Feynman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Feynman "Richard Feynman") give talks on quantum computing. Benioff's talk built on his earlier 1980 work showing that a computer can operate under the laws of quantum mechanics. The talk was titled "Quantum mechanical Hamiltonian models of discrete processes that erase their own histories: application to Turing machines".[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-29) In Feynman's talk, he observed that it appeared to be impossible to efficiently simulate the evolution of a quantum nature system on a classical computer, and he proposed a basic model for a quantum computer.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-30) Feynman's conjecture on a quantum simulating computer, published 1982,[[d]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-31) understood as - the reality of [quantum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics "Quantum mechanics") expressed as an effective quantum system necessitates quantum computers,[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-32) is conventionally accepted as a beginning of quantum computing.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-33)[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-34)

*   Paul Benioff further develops his original model of a quantum mechanical Turing machine.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-35)
*   [William Wootters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Wootters "William Wootters") and [Wojciech H. Zurek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wojciech_H._Zurek "Wojciech H. Zurek"),[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-36) and independently [Dennis Dieks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Dieks "Dennis Dieks")[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-37) rediscover the [no-cloning theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No-cloning_theorem "No-cloning theorem") of James L. Park.

[Charles Bennett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_H._Bennett_(physicist) "Charles H. Bennett (physicist)") and [Gilles Brassard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilles_Brassard "Gilles Brassard") employ Wiesner's conjugate coding for distribution of cryptographic keys.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-38)

*   [David Deutsch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Deutsch "David Deutsch"), at the University of Oxford, England, describes the first [universal quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_quantum_computer "Universal quantum computer"). Just as a [Universal Turing machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Turing_machine "Universal Turing machine") can simulate any other Turing machine efficiently ([Church–Turing thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church%E2%80%93Turing_thesis "Church–Turing thesis")), so the universal quantum computer is able to simulate any other quantum computer with at most a [polynomial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial "Polynomial") slowdown.
*   [Asher Peres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asher_Peres "Asher Peres") points out the need for [quantum error correction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_error_correction "Quantum error correction") schemes and discusses a [repetition code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_error_correction#Bit_flip_code "Quantum error correction") for amplitude errors.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-39)

*   [Yoshihisa Yamamoto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoshihisa_Yamamoto_(scientist) "Yoshihisa Yamamoto (scientist)") and K. Igeta propose the first physical realization of a quantum computer, including Feynman's [CNOT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNOT "CNOT") gate.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-qc1988-40) Their approach uses atoms and photons and is the progenitor of modern quantum computing and networking protocols using photons to transmit qubits and atoms to perform two-qubit operations.

*   [Gerard J. Milburn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerard_J._Milburn "Gerard J. Milburn") proposes a quantum-optical realization of a [Fredkin gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fredkin_gate "Fredkin gate").[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-fredkin1988-41)
*   [Bikas Chakrabarti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bikas_Chakrabarti "Bikas Chakrabarti")& collaborators from [Saha Institute of Nuclear Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saha_Institute_of_Nuclear_Physics "Saha Institute of Nuclear Physics"), Kolkata, India, propose that quantum fluctuations could help explore rugged energy landscapes by escaping from local minima of glassy systems having tall but thin barriers by tunneling (instead of climbing over using thermal excitations), suggesting the effectiveness of [quantum annealing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_annealing "Quantum annealing") over classical [simulated annealing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_annealing "Simulated annealing").[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Chakrabarti89-42)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-43)

[Artur Ekert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artur_Ekert "Artur Ekert") at the University of Oxford, proposes [entanglement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement "Quantum entanglement")-based secure communication.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-44)

*   David Deutsch and Richard Jozsa propose a computational problem that can be solved efficiently with the deterministic [Deutsch–Jozsa algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsch%E2%80%93Jozsa_algorithm "Deutsch–Jozsa algorithm") on a quantum computer, but for which no deterministic classical algorithm is possible. This was perhaps the earliest result in the [computational complexity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity "Computational complexity") of quantum computers, proving that they were capable of performing _some_ well-defined computation more efficiently than any classical computer.
*   [Ethan Bernstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethan_Bernstein&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ethan Bernstein (page does not exist)") and [Umesh Vazirani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umesh_Vazirani "Umesh Vazirani") propose the [Bernstein–Vazirani algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernstein%E2%80%93Vazirani_algorithm "Bernstein–Vazirani algorithm"). It is a restricted version of the Deutsch–Jozsa algorithm where instead of distinguishing between two different classes of functions, it tries to learn a string encoded in a function. The Bernstein–Vazirani algorithm was designed to prove an oracle separation between complexity classes [BQP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BQP "BQP") and [BPP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BPP_(complexity) "BPP (complexity)").
*   Research groups at [Max Planck Institute of Quantum Optics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Quantum_Optics "Max Planck Institute of Quantum Optics") ([Garching](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garching "Garching"))[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-45)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-46) and shortly after at [NIST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NIST "NIST") ([Boulder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado "Boulder, Colorado"))[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-47) experimentally realize the first crystallized strings of [laser-cooled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laser_cooling "Laser cooling") ions. Linear ion crystals constitute the qubit basis for most quantum computing and simulation experiments with trapped ions.

Daniel R. Simon, at [Université de Montréal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Montr%C3%A9al "Université de Montréal"), Quebec, Canada, invent an [oracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_machine "Oracle machine") problem, [Simon's problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon%27s_problem "Simon's problem"), for which a quantum computer would be [exponentially faster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exponential_growth "Exponential growth") than a conventional computer. This [algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm "Algorithm") introduces the main ideas which were then developed in [Peter Shor's factorization algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shor%27s_algorithm "Shor's algorithm").

*   [Peter Shor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Shor "Peter Shor"), at AT&T's [Bell Labs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bell_Labs "Bell Labs") in [New Jersey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Jersey "New Jersey"), publishes [Shor's algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shor%27s_algorithm "Shor's algorithm"). It would allow a quantum computer to factor large integers quickly. It solves both the [factoring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer_factorization "Integer factorization") problem and the [discrete log](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_log "Discrete log") problem. The algorithm can theoretically break many of the [cryptosystems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptosystem "Cryptosystem") in use today. Its invention sparked tremendous interest in quantum computers.
*   The first [United States Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Government "United States Government") workshop on quantum computing is organized by [NIST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NIST "NIST") in [Gaithersburg, Maryland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaithersburg,_Maryland "Gaithersburg, Maryland"), in autumn.
*   [Isaac Chuang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Chuang "Isaac Chuang") and [Yoshihisa Yamamoto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoshihisa_Yamamoto_(scientist) "Yoshihisa Yamamoto (scientist)") propose a quantum-optical realization of a quantum computer to implement Deutsch's algorithm.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-cy1995-48) Their work introduced dual-rail encoding for photonic qubits.
*   In December, [Ignacio Cirac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacio_Cirac "Ignacio Cirac"), at [University of Castilla–La Mancha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Castilla%E2%80%93La_Mancha "University of Castilla–La Mancha") at [Ciudad Real](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciudad_Real "Ciudad Real"), and [Peter Zoller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Zoller "Peter Zoller") at the [University of Innsbruck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Innsbruck "University of Innsbruck") propose an experimental realization of the [controlled NOT gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_NOT_gate "Controlled NOT gate") with [cold trapped ions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ion-trap_quantum_computing "Ion-trap quantum computing").[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-49)

*   The first [United States Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") workshop on quantum computing and [quantum cryptography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_cryptography "Quantum cryptography") is organized by [United States Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army "United States Army") physicists Charles M. Bowden, [Jonathan Dowling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Dowling "Jonathan Dowling"), and [Henry O. Everitt](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry_O._Everitt&action=edit&redlink=1 "Henry O. Everitt (page does not exist)"); it took place in February at the [University of Arizona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Arizona "University of Arizona") in [Tucson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona "Tucson, Arizona").
*   Peter Shor proposes the first schemes for [quantum error correction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_error_correction "Quantum error correction").[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-50)
*   [Christopher Monroe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Monroe "Christopher Monroe") and [David J. Wineland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_J._Wineland "David J. Wineland") at [NIST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NIST "NIST") ([Boulder, Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado "Boulder, Colorado")) experimentally realize the first [quantum logic gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_logic_gate "Quantum logic gate") – [the controlled NOT gate – with trapped ions, following the Cirac-Zoller proposal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cirac%E2%80%93Zoller_controlled-NOT_gate "Cirac–Zoller controlled-NOT gate").[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-51)
*   Independently, [Subhash Kak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subhash_Kak "Subhash Kak") and [Ronald Chrisley](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ronald_Chrisley&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ronald Chrisley (page does not exist)") propose the first [quantum neural network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_neural_network "Quantum neural network").[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-52)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-53)

*   [Lov Grover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lov_Grover "Lov Grover"), at Bell Labs, invents the [quantum database search algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grover%27s_algorithm "Grover's algorithm"). The [quadratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadratic_function "Quadratic function") speedup is not as dramatic as the speedup for factoring, discrete logs, or physics simulations. However, the algorithm can be applied to a much wider variety of problems. Any problem that can be solved by random, brute-force search, may take advantage of this quadratic speedup in the number of search queries.
*   The United States Government, particularly in a joint partnership of the Army Research Office (now part of the [Army Research Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_Research_Laboratory "Army Research Laboratory")) and the [National Security Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Agency "National Security Agency"), issues the first public call for research proposals in quantum information processing.
*   [Andrew Steane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Steane "Andrew Steane") designs [Steane code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steane_code "Steane code") for error correction.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-54)
*   [David DiVincenzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_DiVincenzo "David DiVincenzo"), of IBM, proposes a list of minimal requirements for creating a quantum computer,[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-55) now called [DiVincenzo's criteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DiVincenzo%27s_criteria "DiVincenzo's criteria").
*   [Seth Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seth_Lloyd "Seth Lloyd") proves Feynman's conjecture on quantum simulation.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-56)

*   [David G. Cory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_G._Cory "David G. Cory"), Amr Fahmy and [Timothy Havel](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Timothy_Havel&action=edit&redlink=1 "Timothy Havel (page does not exist)"), and at the same time [Neil Gershenfeld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Gershenfeld "Neil Gershenfeld") and [Isaac Chuang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Chuang "Isaac Chuang") at [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology "Massachusetts Institute of Technology") publish the first papers realizing gates for quantum computers based on bulk nuclear [spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(physics) "Spin (physics)") resonance, or thermal ensembles. The technology is based on a [nuclear magnetic resonance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance "Nuclear magnetic resonance") (NMR) machine, which is similar to the medical [magnetic resonance imaging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging "Magnetic resonance imaging") machine.
*   [Alexei Kitaev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexei_Kitaev "Alexei Kitaev") describes the principles of [topological quantum computation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topological_quantum_computer "Topological quantum computer") as a method for dealing with the problem of [decoherence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_decoherence "Quantum decoherence").[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-57)
*   [Daniel Loss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Loss "Daniel Loss") and David DiVincenzo propose the [Loss-DiVincenzo quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loss-DiVincenzo_quantum_computer "Loss-DiVincenzo quantum computer"), using as qubits the intrinsic [spin-1/2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin-1/2 "Spin-1/2") degree of freedom of individual electrons confined to [quantum dots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_dot "Quantum dot").[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-58)

*   The first experimental demonstration of a quantum algorithm is reported. A working 2-qubit [NMR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance "Nuclear magnetic resonance") quantum computer was used to solve Deutsch's problem by [Jonathan A. Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_A._Jones "Jonathan A. Jones") and [Michele Mosca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michele_Mosca "Michele Mosca") at Oxford University and shortly after by Isaac L. Chuang at [IBM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM "IBM")'s [Almaden Research Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almaden_Research_Center "Almaden Research Center"), in California, and Mark Kubinec and the University of California, Berkeley together with coworkers at [Stanford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University") in California and [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology "Massachusetts Institute of Technology") in Massachusetts.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-59)
*   The first working 3-qubit NMR computer is reported.
*   Bruce Kane proposes a silicon-based [nuclear spin quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kane_quantum_computer "Kane quantum computer"), using nuclear spins of individual phosphorus atoms in silicon as the qubits and donor electrons to mediate the coupling between qubits.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-60)
*   The first execution of [Grover's algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grover%27s_algorithm "Grover's algorithm") on an NMR computer is reported.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-61)
*   Hidetoshi Nishimori & colleagues from [Tokyo Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tokyo_Institute_of_Technology "Tokyo Institute of Technology") show that a [quantum annealing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_annealing "Quantum annealing") algorithm can perform better than classical [simulated annealing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_annealing "Simulated annealing") under certain conditions.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-62)
*   [Daniel Gottesman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Gottesman "Daniel Gottesman") and Emanuel Knill independently prove that a certain subclass of quantum computations can be efficiently emulated with classical resources ([Gottesman–Knill theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gottesman%E2%80%93Knill_theorem "Gottesman–Knill theorem")).[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-63)

*   [Samuel L. Braunstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_L._Braunstein "Samuel L. Braunstein") and collaborators show that none of the bulk NMR experiments performed to date contain any entanglement; the quantum states being too strongly mixed. This is seen as evidence that NMR computers would likely not yield a benefit over classical computers. It remains an open question, however, whether entanglement is necessary for quantum computational speedup.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-64)
*   [Gabriel Aeppli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Aeppli "Gabriel Aeppli"), [Thomas Rosenbaum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Rosenbaum "Thomas Rosenbaum") and colleagues demonstrate experimentally the basic concepts of quantum annealing in a condensed matter system.
*   [Yasunobu Nakamura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasunobu_Nakamura "Yasunobu Nakamura") and [Jaw-Shen Tsai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaw-Shen_Tsai "Jaw-Shen Tsai") demonstrate that a [superconducting circuit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superconducting_quantum_computing "Superconducting quantum computing") can be used as a qubit.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-nt1999-65)

*   [Arun K. Pati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arun_K._Pati "Arun K. Pati") and Samuel L. Braunstein prove the [quantum no-deleting theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_no-deleting_theorem "Quantum no-deleting theorem"). This is dual to the no-cloning theorem which shows that one cannot delete a copy of an unknown qubit. Together with the stronger no-cloning theorem, the no-deleting theorem has the implication that quantum information can neither be created nor be destroyed.
*   The first working 5-qubit NMR computer is demonstrated at the [Technical University of Munich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technical_University_of_Munich "Technical University of Munich"), Germany.
*   The first execution of order finding (part of Shor's algorithm) at IBM's Almaden Research Center and Stanford University is demonstrated.
*   The first working 7-qubit NMR computer is demonstrated at the [Los Alamos National Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory "Los Alamos National Laboratory") in New Mexico.
*   The textbook, _[Quantum Computation and Quantum Information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum\_Computation\_and\_Quantum\_Information "Quantum Computation and Quantum Information")_, by [Michael Nielsen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Nielsen "Michael Nielsen") and [Isaac Chuang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Chuang "Isaac Chuang") is published.

*   The first execution of Shor's algorithm at IBM's Almaden Research Center and Stanford University is demonstrated. The number 15 was factored using 10 18 identical molecules, each containing seven active nuclear spins.
*   [Noah Linden](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Noah_Linden&action=edit&redlink=1 "Noah Linden (page does not exist)") and [Sandu Popescu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandu_Popescu "Sandu Popescu") prove that the presence of entanglement is a necessary condition for a large class of quantum protocols. This, coupled with Braunstein's result (see 1999 above), called the validity of NMR quantum computation into question.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-66)
*   Emanuel Knill, [Raymond Laflamme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Laflamme "Raymond Laflamme"), and Gerard Milburn show that [optical quantum computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_optical_quantum_computing "Linear optical quantum computing") is possible with single-photon sources, linear optical elements, and single-photon detectors, establishing the field of linear optical quantum computing.
*   Robert Raussendorf and [Hans Jürgen Briegel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_J%C3%BCrgen_Briegel "Hans Jürgen Briegel") propose [measurement-based quantum computation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-way_quantum_computer "One-way quantum computer").[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-67)

*   The Quantum Information Science and Technology Roadmapping Project, involving some of the main participants in the field, lays out the Quantum computation roadmap.
*   The [Institute for Quantum Computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Computing "Institute for Quantum Computing") is established at the [University of Waterloo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Waterloo "University of Waterloo") in Waterloo, Ontario by [Mike Lazaridis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Lazaridis "Mike Lazaridis"), [Raymond Laflamme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Laflamme "Raymond Laflamme") and [Michele Mosca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michele_Mosca "Michele Mosca").[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-68)
*   A group led by Gerhard Birkl (now at TU Darmstadt) demonstrates the first 2D array of optical tweezers with trapped atoms for quantum computation with atomic qubits.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-link.aps.org-69)

*   Implementation of the [Deutsch–Jozsa algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsch%E2%80%93Jozsa_algorithm "Deutsch–Jozsa algorithm") on an ion-trap quantum computer at the [University of Innsbruck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Innsbruck "University of Innsbruck") is reported.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Nat-20030102-70)
*   [Todd D. Pittman](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Todd_D._Pittman&action=edit&redlink=1 "Todd D. Pittman (page does not exist)") and collaborators at [Johns Hopkins University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University "Johns Hopkins University"), [Applied Physics Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_Physics_Laboratory "Applied Physics Laboratory"), and independently [Jeremy O'Brien](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_O%27Brien "Jeremy O'Brien") and collaborators at the [University of Queensland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Queensland "University of Queensland"), demonstrate quantum controlled NOT gates using only linear optical elements.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-71)[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-72)
*   The first implementation of a CNOT quantum gate, according to the Cirac–Zoller proposal, is reported by a team at the University of Innsbruck led by [Rainer Blatt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainer_Blatt "Rainer Blatt").[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Nat-20030327-73)
*   The United States government [DARPA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DARPA "DARPA")[Quantum Network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_network "Quantum network") becomes fully operational on October 23, 2003.
*   The [Institute for Quantum Optics and Quantum Information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Optics_and_Quantum_Information "Institute for Quantum Optics and Quantum Information") (IQOQI) is established in Innsbruck and Vienna, Austria, by the founding directors [Rainer Blatt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainer_Blatt "Rainer Blatt"), [Hans Jürgen Briegel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_J%C3%BCrgen_Briegel "Hans Jürgen Briegel"), [Rudolf Grimm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolf_Grimm "Rudolf Grimm"), [Anton Zeilinger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anton_Zeilinger "Anton Zeilinger") and [Peter Zoller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Zoller "Peter Zoller").

*   The first working [pure state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_state "Pure state") NMR quantum computer (based on [parahydrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthohydrogen "Orthohydrogen")) is demonstrated at [Oxford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Oxford "University of Oxford") and [University of York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_York "University of York") in England.
*   Physicists at the University of Innsbruck show deterministic quantum-state teleportation between a pair of trapped calcium ions.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-NAT-20040617-74)
*   The first five-photon entanglement is demonstrated by [Pan Jianwei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan_Jianwei "Pan Jianwei")'s team at the University of Science and Technology of China; the minimal number of qubits required for universal quantum error correction.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-75)

*   [University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Urbana-Champaign "University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign") scientists demonstrate quantum entanglement of multiple characteristics, potentially allowing multiple qubits per particle.
*   Two teams of physicists measure the capacitance of a [Josephson junction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josephson_junction "Josephson junction") for the first time. The methods could be used to measure the state of quantum bits in a quantum computer without disturbing the state.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-76)
*   In December, [W states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W_state "W state") of [quantum registers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_register "Quantum register") with up to 8 qubits implemented using [trapped ions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trapped_ion_quantum_computing "Trapped ion quantum computing") are demonstrated at the [Institute for Quantum Optics and Quantum Information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Optics_and_Quantum_Information "Institute for Quantum Optics and Quantum Information") and the University of Innsbruck in Austria.[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-77)
*   [Harvard University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University "Harvard University") and [Georgia Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Institute_of_Technology "Georgia Institute of Technology") (US) researchers succeed in transferring quantum information between "quantum memories" – from atoms to photons and back again.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

*   The Materials Science Department of Oxford University, England cage a qubit in a "buckyball" (a molecule of [buckminsterfullerene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buckminsterfullerene "Buckminsterfullerene")) and demonstrated quantum "bang-bang" error correction.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-78)
*   Researchers from the [University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Urbana-Champaign "University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign") use the [Zeno Effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_Zeno_effect "Quantum Zeno effect"), repeatedly measuring the properties of a photon to gradually change it without actually allowing the photon to reach the program, to search a database using [counterfactual quantum computation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterfactual_quantum_computation "Counterfactual quantum computation").[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-79)
*   [Vlatko Vedral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlatko_Vedral "Vlatko Vedral") of the University of Leeds, England and colleagues at the universities of Porto and Vienna find that the photons in ordinary laser light can be quantum mechanically entangled with the vibrations of a macroscopic mirror.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-80)
*   [Samuel L. Braunstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_L._Braunstein "Samuel L. Braunstein") at the [University of York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_York "University of York"), North Yorkshire, England, along with the University of Tokyo and the Japan Science and Technology Agency give the first experimental demonstration of quantum telecloning.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-81)
*   Professors at the [University of Sheffield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Sheffield "University of Sheffield"), England, develop a means to efficiently produce and manipulate individual photons at high efficiency at room temperature.[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-82)
*   A new error checking method is theorized for Josephson junction computers.[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-83)
*   The first 12-qubit quantum computer is benchmarked by researchers at the [Institute for Quantum Computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Computing "Institute for Quantum Computing") and the [Perimeter Institute for Theoretical Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perimeter_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics "Perimeter Institute for Theoretical Physics") in Waterloo, Ontario as well as at [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT "MIT"), Cambridge, Massachusetts.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-84)
*   A two-dimensional ion trap is developed for quantum computing.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-85)
*   Seven atoms are placed in a stable line, a step on the way to constructing a quantum gate, at the University of Bonn, Germany.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-86)
*   A team at [Delft University of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delft_University_of_Technology "Delft University of Technology") in the Netherlands creates a device that can manipulate the "up" or "down" spin-states of electrons on quantum dots.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-87)
*   The [University of Arkansas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Arkansas "University of Arkansas") develops quantum dot molecules.[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-88)
*   The spinning new theory on particle spin brings science closer to quantum computing.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-89)
*   The [University of Copenhagen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Copenhagen "University of Copenhagen"), Denmark, develops quantum teleportation between photons and atoms.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-spooky20061004-90)
*   [University of Camerino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Camerino "University of Camerino") scientists develop a theory of macroscopic object entanglement, which has implications for the development of [quantum repeaters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_network#Repeaters "Quantum network").[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-91)
*   Tai-Chang Chiang, at Illinois at Urbana–Champaign, finds that quantum coherence can be maintained in mixed-material systems.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-92)
*   Cristophe Boehme, University of Utah, demonstrates the feasibility of reading data using the [nuclear spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_spin "Nuclear spin") on a silicon-phosphorus [Kane quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kane_quantum_computer "Kane quantum computer").[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-93)

*   Subwavelength waveguide is developed for light.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-94)
*   A single-photon emitter for optical fibers is developed.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-95)
*   The first [one-way quantum computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-way_quantum_computer "One-way quantum computer") are built,[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-96) where [measurement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_measurement "Quantum measurement") ([collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave_function_collapse "Wave function collapse")) of an [entangled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement "Quantum entanglement")[cluster state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cluster_state "Cluster state") is the main driving force of computation,[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-97) and shown to perform simple computations, such as [Deutsch's algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsch%27s_algorithm "Deutsch's algorithm").[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-98)
*   A new material is proposed for quantum computing.[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-99)
*   A single-atom single-photon server is devised.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-100)
*   The University of Cambridge, England, develops an electron quantum pump.[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-101)
*   A superior method of qubit coupling is developed.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-102)
*   A successful demonstration of controllably [coupled qubits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_coupling "Quantum coupling") is reported.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-103)
*   A breakthrough in applying [spin-based electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spintronics "Spintronics") to [silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon "Silicon") is reported.[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-104)
*   Scientists demonstrate a quantum state exchange between light and matter.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-105)
*   A diamond [quantum register](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_register "Quantum register") is developed.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-106)
*   Controlled NOT quantum gates on a pair of superconducting quantum bits are realized.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-107)
*   Scientists contain and study hundreds of individual atoms in 3D array.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-108)
*   Nitrogen in a [buckyball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buckyball "Buckyball") molecule is used in quantum computing.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-109)
*   A large number of electrons are quantum coupled.[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-110)
*   [Spin–orbit interaction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin%E2%80%93orbit_interaction "Spin–orbit interaction") of electrons are measured.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-111)
*   Atoms are quantum manipulated in laser light.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-112)
*   Light pulses are used to control electron spins.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-113)
*   Quantum effects are demonstrated across tens of nanometers.[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-114)
*   Light pulses are used to accelerate quantum computing development.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-115)
*   A quantum random access memory (RAM) blueprint is unveiled.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-116)
*   A model of a quantum transistor is developed.[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-117)
*   Long distance entanglement is demonstrated.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-118)
*   Photonic quantum computing is used to factor a number by two independent labs.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-119)
*   A quantum bus is developed by two independent labs.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-120)
*   A superconducting quantum cable is developed.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-121)
*   The transmission of qubits is demonstrated.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-122)
*   Superior qubit material is devised.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-123)
*   A single-electron qubit memory is reported.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-124)
*   [Bose–Einstein condensate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate "Bose–Einstein condensate")[quantum memory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_memory "Quantum memory") is developed.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-125)
*   [D-Wave Systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-Wave_Systems "D-Wave Systems") demonstrates use of a 28-qubit quantum annealing computer.[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-126)
*   A new cryonic method reduces decoherence and increases interaction distance, and thus quantum computing speed.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-127)
*   A photonic quantum computer is demonstrated.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-128)
*   Graphene quantum dot spin qubits are proposed.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-129)

[![Image 2](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DWave_128chip.jpg/250px-DWave_128chip.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:DWave_128chip.jpg)

Chip constructed by D-Wave Systems Inc. designed to operate as a 128-qubit superconducting adiabatic quantum optimization processor, mounted in a sample holder (2009)

*   The [HHL algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HHL_algorithm "HHL algorithm") for solving linear equations is published.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-130)
*   [Graphene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphene "Graphene") quantum dot qubits are described.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-131)
*   Scientists succeed in storing a quantum bit.[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-132)
*   3D qubit-qutrit entanglement is demonstrated.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-133)
*   Analog quantum computing is devised.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-134)
*   Control of quantum tunneling is devised.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-135)
*   Entangled memory is developed.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-136)
*   A superior NOT gate is developed.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-137)
*   [Qutrits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qutrit "Qutrit") are developed.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-138)
*   Quantum logic gate in optical fiber is reported.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-139)
*   A superior [quantum Hall Effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_Hall_effect "Quantum Hall effect") is discovered.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-140)
*   Enduring spin states in quantum dots are reported.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-141)
*   Molecular magnets are proposed for quantum RAM.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-142)
*   Quasiparticles offer hope of stable quantum computers.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-143)
*   Image storage may have better storage of qubits is reported.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-144)
*   Quantum entangled images are reported.[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-145)
*   Quantum state is intentionally altered in a molecule.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-146)
*   Electron position is controlled in a silicon circuit.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-147)
*   A superconducting electronic circuit pumps microwave photons.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-148)
*   Amplitude spectroscopy is developed.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-149)
*   A superior quantum computer test is developed.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-150)
*   An optical frequency comb is devised.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-151)
*   The concept of [Quantum Darwinism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_Darwinism "Quantum Darwinism") is supported.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-152)
*   Hybrid qubit memory is developed.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-153)
*   A qubit is stored for over 1 second in an atomic nucleus.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-154)
*   Faster electron spin qubit switching and reading is developed.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-155)
*   The possibility of non-entanglement quantum computing is described.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-156)
*   [D-Wave Systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-Wave_Systems "D-Wave Systems") claims to have produced a 128-qubit computer chip, though this claim had yet to be verified.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-157)

*   [Carbon 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon-12 "Carbon-12") is purified for longer coherence times.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-158)
*   The lifetime of qubits is extended to hundreds of milliseconds.[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-159)
*   Improved quantum control of photons is reported.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-160)
*   Quantum entanglement is demonstrated over 240 micrometres.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-161)
*   Qubit lifetime is extended by a factor of 1000.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-162)
*   The first electronic quantum processor is created.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-163)
*   Six-photon graph state entanglement is used to simulate the fractional statistics of [anyons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anyon "Anyon") living in artificial spin-lattice models.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-164)
*   A single-molecule optical transistor is devised.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-165)
*   [NIST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology "National Institute of Standards and Technology") reads and writes individual qubits.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-166)
*   NIST demonstrates multiple computing operations on qubits.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-167)
*   The first large-scale topological cluster state quantum architecture is developed for atom-optics.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-168)
*   A combination of all of the fundamental elements required to perform scalable quantum computing through the use of qubits stored in the internal states of trapped atomic ions is shown.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-169)
*   Researchers at University of Bristol, U.K., demonstrate Shor's algorithm on a silicon photonic chip.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-170)
*   Quantum Computing with an Electron Spin Ensemble is reported.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-171)
*   A so-called photon machine gun is developed for quantum computing.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-172)
*   The first universal programmable quantum computer is unveiled.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-173)
*   Scientists electrically control quantum states of electrons.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-174)
*   Google collaborates with D-Wave Systems on image search technology using quantum computing.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-175)
*   A method for synchronizing the properties of multiple coupled CJJ rf-SQUID flux qubits with a small spread of device parameters due to fabrication variations is demonstrated.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-176)
*   Universal Ion Trap Quantum Computation with decoherence free qubits is realized.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-177)
*   The first chip-scale quantum computer is reported.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-178)

*   Ions are trapped in an optical trap.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-179)
*   An optical quantum computer with three qubits calculates the energy spectrum of molecular hydrogen to high precision.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-180)
*   The first germanium laser advances the state of optical computers.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-181)
*   A single-electron qubit is developed[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-182)
*   The quantum state in a macroscopic object is reported.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-183)
*   A new quantum computer cooling method is developed.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-184)
*   Racetrack ion trap is developed.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-185)
*   Evidence for a Moore-Read state in the ![Image 3: {\displaystyle u=5/2}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7e6cf610862620b1f80d912258f14236a51a034b) quantum Hall plateau,[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-186) which would be suitable for topological quantum computation is reported
*   A quantum interface between a single photon and a single atom is demonstrated.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-187)
*   LED (light emitting diode) quantum entanglement is demonstrated.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-188)
*   Multiplexed design increases the speed of transmission of quantum information through a quantum communications channel.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-189)
*   A two-photon optical chip is reported.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-190)
*   Microfabricated planar ion traps are tested.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-191)[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-192)
*   A [boson sampling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boson_sampling "Boson sampling") technique is proposed by Aaronson and Arkhipov.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-193)
*   [Quantum dot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_dot "Quantum dot") qubits are manipulated electrically, not magnetically.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-194)

*   Entanglement in a solid-state spin ensemble is reported[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-195)
*   NOON photons in a superconducting quantum integrated circuit are reported.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-196)
*   A quantum antenna is described.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-197)
*   Multimode quantum interference is documented.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-198)
*   Magnetic Resonance applied to quantum computing is reported.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-199)
*   The quantum pen for single atoms is documented.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-200)
*   Atomic "Racing Dual" is reported.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-201)
*   A 14-qubit register is reported.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-202)
*   D-Wave claims to have developed quantum annealing and introduces their product called D-Wave One. The company claims this is the first commercially available quantum computer.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-203)
*   Repetitive error correction is demonstrated in a quantum processor.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-204)
*   Diamond quantum computer memory is demonstrated.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-205)
*   Qmodes are developed.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-206)
*   Decoherence is demonstrated as suppressed.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-207)
*   Simplification of controlled operations is reported.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-208)
*   Ions entangled using microwaves are documented.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-209)
*   Practical error rates are achieved.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-210)
*   A quantum computer employing [Von Neumann architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_architecture "Von Neumann architecture") is described.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-211)
*   A quantum spin Hall topological insulator is reported.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-212)
*   The concept of two diamonds linked by quantum entanglement could help develop photonic processors is described.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-213)

*   D-Wave claims a quantum computation using 84 qubits.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-214)
*   Physicists create a working transistor from a single atom.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-215)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-216)
*   A method for manipulating the charge of nitrogen vacancy-centres in diamond is reported.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-217)
*   Creation of a 300 qubit/particle quantum simulator is reported.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-218)[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-219)
*   Demonstration of topologically protected qubits with an eight-photon entanglement is reported; a robust approach to practical quantum computing.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-220)
*   [1QB Information Technologies (1QBit)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1QB_Information_Technologies_(1QBit) "1QB Information Technologies (1QBit)") is founded; the world's first dedicated quantum computing software company.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-221)
*   The first design of a quantum repeater system without a need for quantum memories is reported.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-222)
*   Decoherence suppressed for 2 seconds at room temperature by manipulating [Carbon-13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon-13 "Carbon-13") atoms with lasers is reported.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-223)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-224)
*   The theory of Bell-based randomness expansion with reduced assumption of measurement independence is reported.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-225)
*   New low overhead method for fault-tolerant quantum logic is developed called lattice surgery.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-226)

*   Coherence time of 39 minutes at room temperature (and 3 hours at cryogenic temperatures) is demonstrated for an ensemble of impurity-spin qubits in isotopically purified silicon.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-39_minutes-227)
*   Extension of time for a qubit maintained in superimposed state for ten times longer than what has ever been achieved before is reported.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-228)
*   The first resource analysis of a large-scale quantum algorithm using explicit fault-tolerant, error-correction protocols is developed for factoring.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-229)

*   Documents leaked by [Edward Snowden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Snowden "Edward Snowden") confirm the [Penetrating Hard Targets project](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Penetrating_Hard_Targets_project&action=edit&redlink=1 "Penetrating Hard Targets project (page does not exist)"),[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-230) by which the US [National Security Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Agency "National Security Agency") sought to develop a quantum computing capability for [cryptography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography "Cryptography") purposes.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-231)[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-232)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-233)
*   Researchers in Japan and Austria publish the first large-scale quantum computing architecture for a diamond-based system.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-234)
*   Scientists at the University of Innsbruck perform quantum computations on a topologically encoded qubit which is encoded in entangled states distributed over seven trapped-ion qubits.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-SCI-20140718-235)
*   Scientists transfer data by [quantum teleportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_teleportation "Quantum teleportation") over a distance of 10 feet (3.0 meters) with zero percent error rate; a vital step towards a quantum Internet.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-NYT-20140529-236)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-SCI-20140529-237)

*   Optically addressable nuclear spins in a solid with a six-hour coherence time are documented.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-238)
*   Quantum information encoded by simple electrical pulses is documented.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-239)
*   Quantum error detection code using a square lattice of four superconducting qubits is documented.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-240)
*   D-Wave Systems Incorporated announce on June 22 that it had broken the 1,000-qubit barrier.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-241)
*   A two-qubit silicon logic gate is successfully developed.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-242)

*   Physicists led by Rainer Blatt join forces with scientists at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology (MIT), led by Isaac Chuang, to efficiently implement Shor's algorithm in an ion-trap-based quantum computer.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-243)
*   IBM releases the Quantum Experience, an online interface to their superconducting systems. The system is immediately used to publish new protocols in quantum information processing.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-244)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-245)
*   Google, using an array of 9 superconducting qubits developed by the [Martinis group](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Martinis_group&action=edit&redlink=1 "Martinis group (page does not exist)") and [UCSB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara "University of California, Santa Barbara"), simulates a [hydrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen "Hydrogen") molecule.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-246)
*   Scientists in Japan and Australia invent a quantum version of a [Sneakernet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sneakernet "Sneakernet") communications system.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-247)

*   D-Wave Systems Incorporated announce general commercial availability of the D-Wave 2000Q quantum annealer, which it claims has 2000 qubits.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-248)
*   A blueprint for a microwave trapped ion quantum computer is published.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-249)
*   IBM unveils a 17-qubit quantum computer—and a better way of benchmarking it.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-250)
*   Scientists build a microchip that generates two entangled [qudits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qudit "Qudit") each with 10 states, for 100 dimensions total.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-251)
*   Microsoft revealed [Q#](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Q_Sharp "Q Sharp"), a quantum programming language integrated with its [Visual Studio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_Studio "Visual Studio") development environment. Programs can be executed locally on a 32-qubit simulator, or a 40-qubit simulator on [Azure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azure_DevOps_Server "Azure DevOps Server").[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-252)
*   IBM reveals a working 50-qubit quantum computer that maintains its quantum state for 90 microseconds.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-253)
*   The first [teleportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_teleportation "Quantum teleportation") using a satellite, connecting ground stations over a distance of 1400 km apart is announced.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-254) Previous experiments were at [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth"), at shorter distances.

*   [John Preskill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Preskill "John Preskill") introduces the concept of [noisy intermediate-scale quantum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noisy_intermediate-scale_quantum_era "Noisy intermediate-scale quantum era") (NISQ) era.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-255)
*   MIT scientists report the discovery of a new triple-photon form of [light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light "Light").[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-NW-20180216-256)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-SCI-20180216-257)
*   Oxford researchers successfully use a trapped-ion technique, where they place two charged atoms in a state of quantum entanglement to speed up logic gates by a factor of 20 to 60 times, as compared with the previous best gates, translated to 1.6 microseconds long, with 99.8% precision.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-258)
*   QuTech successfully tests a silicon-based 2-spin-qubit processor.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-259)[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-260)
*   Google announces the creation of a 72-qubit quantum chip, called "Bristlecone",[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-261) achieving a new record.
*   Intel announces the fabrication and testing of silicon-based spin-qubit processors manufactured in the company's D1D fab in Oregon.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-262)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-263)
*   Intel confirms development of a 49-qubit superconducting test chip, called "Tangle Lake".[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-264)
*   Japanese researchers demonstrate universal holonomic quantum gates.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-265)
*   An integrated photonic platform for quantum information with continuous variables is documented.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-266)
*   On December 17, 2018, the company IonQ introduces the first commercial trapped-ion quantum computer, with a program length of over 60 two-qubit gates, 11 fully connected qubits, 55 addressable pairs, one-qubit gate error of <0.03% and two-qubit gate error of <1.0%.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-267)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-268)
*   On December 21, 2018, the US [National Quantum Initiative Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Quantum_Initiative_Act "National Quantum Initiative Act") was signed into law by US [President](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States "President of the United States")[Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"), establishing the goals and priorities for a 10-year plan to accelerate the development of quantum information science and technology applications in the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States").[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-govtrack-269)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-270)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-271)

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/IBM_Q_system_%28Fraunhofer_2%29.jpg/330px-IBM_Q_system_%28Fraunhofer_2%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IBM_Q_system_(Fraunhofer_2).jpg)

[IBM Q System One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Q_System_One "IBM Q System One") (2019), the first circuit-based commercial quantum computer
