*   IBM unveils its first commercial quantum computer, the [IBM Q System One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Q_System_One "IBM Q System One"),[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-272) designed by UK-based [Map Project Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Map_Project_Office "Map Project Office") and Universal Design Studio and manufactured by Goppion.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-273)
*   Austrian physicists demonstrate self-verifying, hybrid, variational quantum simulation of lattice models in condensed matter and high-energy physics using a feedback loop between a classical computer and a quantum co-processor.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Nat-20190515-274)
*   Griffith University, University of New South Wales (UNSW), Sydney, Australia, and UTS, in partnership with seven universities in the United States, develop noise cancelling for quantum bits via machine learning, taking quantum noise in a quantum chip down to 0%.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-275)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-276)
*   [Quantum Darwinism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_Darwinism "Quantum Darwinism") is observed in diamond at room temperature.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-PRL-20191001-277)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Science-20190913-278)
*   Google reveals its [Sycamore processor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sycamore_processor "Sycamore processor"), consisting of 53 qubits. A paper by Google's quantum computer research team is briefly available in late September 2019, claiming the project had reached [quantum supremacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_supremacy "Quantum supremacy").[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-279)[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-280)[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-281) Google also develops a cryogenic chip for controlling qubits from within a dilution refrigerator.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-282)
*   [University of Science and Technology of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Science_and_Technology_of_China "University of Science and Technology of China") researchers demonstrate boson sampling with 14 detected photons.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-283)

*   20 April – UNSW Sydney develops a way of producing 'hot qubits' – quantum devices that operate at 1.5 kelvin.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-284)
*   11 March – UNSW perform electric nuclear resonance to control single atoms in electronic devices.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-285)
*   23 April – University of Tokyo and Australian scientists create and successfully test a solution to the quantum wiring problem, creating a 2D structure for qubits. Such structure can be built using existing integrated circuit technology and has considerably lower cross-talk.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-286)
*   16 January – Quantum physicists report the first direct splitting of one photon into three using [spontaneous parametric down-conversion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spontaneous_parametric_down-conversion "Spontaneous parametric down-conversion") which may have applications in [quantum technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_technology "Quantum technology").[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-287)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-288)
*   11 February – Quantum engineers report that they created [artificial atoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_atom "Artificial atom") in [silicon quantum dots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon_quantum_dot "Silicon quantum dot") for [quantum computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computing "Quantum computing") and that artificial atoms with a higher number of electrons can be more stable qubits than previously thought possible. Enabling [silicon-based quantum computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_qubit_quantum_computer "Spin qubit quantum computer") may make it possible to reuse the manufacturing technology of "classical" modern-day computer chips among other advantages.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-289)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-290)
*   14 February – Quantum physicists develop a novel [single-photon source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-photon_source "Single-photon source") which may allow bridging of semiconductor-based quantum-computers that use photons by converting the state of an electron [spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(physics) "Spin (physics)") to the [polarisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polarization_(waves) "Polarization (waves)") of a photon. They showed that they can generate a single photon in a controlled way without the need for [randomly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random "Random") formed [quantum dots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_dot_single-photon_source "Quantum dot single-photon source") or structural defects in diamonds.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-291)[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-292)
*   25 February – Scientists visualize a [quantum measurement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_measurement "Quantum measurement"): by taking snapshots of ion states at different times of measurement via coupling of a trapped ion [qutrit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qutrit "Qutrit") to the photon environment, they showed that the changes of the degrees of [superpositions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_superposition "Quantum superposition"), and therefore of [probabilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilities "Probabilities") of states after measurement, happens gradually under the measurement influence.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-293)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-294)
*   [![Image 5](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/IQM_Quantum_Computer_Espoo_Finland.jpg/250px-IQM_Quantum_Computer_Espoo_Finland.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IQM_Quantum_Computer_Espoo_Finland.jpg)

Working IQM Quantum Computer installed in Espoo, Finland in 2020

2 March – Scientists report achieving repeated [quantum nondemolition measurements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_nondemolition_measurement "Quantum nondemolition measurement") of an electron's spin in a silicon quantum dot: measurements that do not change the electron's spin in the process.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-295)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-296)
*   11 March – Quantum engineers report to have controlled the nucleus of a single atom using only electric fields. This was first suggested to be possible in 1961 and may be used for silicon [quantum computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computer "Quantum computer") that use single-atom spins without needing oscillating magnetic fields. This may be especially useful for [nanodevices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanodevice "Nanodevice"), for precise sensors of electric and magnetic fields, as well as for fundamental inquiries into [quantum nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_physics "Quantum physics").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-297)[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-298)
*   19 March – A US Army laboratory announces that its scientists analysed a [Rydberg sensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rydberg_atom#Current_research_directions "Rydberg atom")'s sensitivity to oscillating electric fields over an enormous range of frequencies—from 0 to 10^12 [Hz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hertz "Hertz") (the spectrum to 0.3 mm wavelength). The Rydberg sensor may potentially be used to detect communications signals as it could reliably detect signals over the entire spectrum and compare favourably with other established electric field sensor technologies, such as electro-optic crystals and dipole antenna-coupled passive electronics.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-2020-03-19_Phys-299)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-300)
*   23 March – Researchers report that they corrected for [signal loss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attenuation#Electromagnetic "Attenuation") in a prototype quantum [node](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(networking) "Node (networking)") that can catch, store and entangle bits of quantum information. Their concepts could be used for key components of [quantum repeaters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_repeater "Quantum repeater") in quantum networks and extend their longest possible range.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-301)[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-302)
*   15 April – Researchers demonstrate a proof-of-concept silicon quantum processor unit cell which works at 1.5 kelvin – many times warmer than common quantum processors that are being developed. The finding may enable the integration of classical control electronics with a qubit array and substantially reduce costs. The cooling requirements necessary for quantum computing have been called one of the toughest roadblocks in the field.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-303)[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-304)[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-305)[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-306)
*   16 April – Scientists prove the existence of the [Rashba effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashba_effect "Rashba effect") in bulk [perovskites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perovskite "Perovskite"). Previously researchers have hypothesized that the materials' extraordinary electronic, magnetic and optical properties – which make it a commonly used material [for solar cells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perovskite_solar_cell "Perovskite solar cell") and [quantum electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perovskite_nanocrystal "Perovskite nanocrystal") – are related to this effect which to date had not been proven to be present in the material.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-307)[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-308)
*   8 May – Researchers report to have developed a proof-of-concept of a [quantum radar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_radar "Quantum radar") using quantum entanglement and [microwaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microwave "Microwave") which may potentially be useful for the development of improved radar systems, security scanners and medical imaging systems.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-309)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-310)[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-311)
*   12 May – Researchers report to have developed a method to selectively manipulate a layered [manganite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manganite "Manganite")'s [correlated electrons'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_correlation "Electronic correlation") spin state while leaving its [orbital state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_orbital "Atomic orbital") intact using [femtosecond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultrashort_pulse "Ultrashort pulse")[X-ray laser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-ray_laser "X-ray laser") pulses. This may indicate that [orbitronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orbitronics&action=edit&redlink=1 "Orbitronics (page does not exist)") – using variations in the orientations of orbitals – may be used as the [basic unit of information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit "Bit") in novel information technology devices.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-312)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-313)
*   19 May – Researchers report to have developed the first integrated silicon on-chip low-noise [single-photon source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-photon_source "Single-photon source") compatible with large-scale [quantum photonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_quantum_photonics "Integrated quantum photonics").[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-314)[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-315)[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-316)
*   11 June – Scientists report the generation of [rubidium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubidium "Rubidium")[Bose–Einstein condensates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate "Bose–Einstein condensate") (BECs) in the [Cold Atom Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_Atom_Laboratory "Cold Atom Laboratory") aboard the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") under [microgravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microgravity "Microgravity") which could enable improved research of BECs and [quantum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics "Quantum mechanics"), whose physics are scaled to macroscopic scales in BECs, support long-term investigations of [few-body physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Few-body_systems "Few-body systems"), support the development of techniques for [atom–wave interferometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom_interferometer "Atom interferometer") and [atom lasers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom_laser "Atom laser") and verified the successful operation of the laboratory.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-cal-iss-317)[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-318)[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-319)
*   15 June – Scientists report the development of the smallest [synthetic molecular motor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synthetic_molecular_motor "Synthetic molecular motor"), consisting of 12 atoms and a rotor of 4 atoms, shown to be capable of being powered by an electric current using an electron scanning microscope and moving with very low amounts of energy due to [quantum tunneling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_tunneling "Quantum tunneling").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-320)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-321)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-322)
*   17 June – Quantum scientists report the development of a system that entangled two photon [quantum communication nodes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information_science "Quantum information science") through a microwave cable that can send information in between without the photons being sent through, or occupying, the cable. On 12 June it was reported that they also, for the first time, entangled two [phonons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phonon "Phonon") as well as erase information from their measurement after the measurement had been completed using [delayed-choice quantum erasure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delayed-choice_quantum_eraser "Delayed-choice quantum eraser").[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-323)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-324)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-325)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-326)
*   18 June – Honeywell announces a quantum computer with a quantum volume of 64, the highest at the time.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-327)
*   13 August – Universal coherence protection is reported to have been achieved in a solid-state spin qubit, a modification that allows quantum systems to stay operational (or "[coherent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_coherence "Quantum coherence")") for 10,000 times longer than before.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-328)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Miao_Blanton_Anderson_Bourassa_2020-329)
*   26 August – Scientists report that ionizing radiation from environmental radioactive materials and [cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_ray "Cosmic ray") may substantially limit the [coherence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_decoherence "Quantum decoherence") times of qubits if they are not adequately [shielded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation_hardening "Radiation hardening").[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-330)[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-331)[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-332)
*   [![Image 6](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Google_Sycamore_Chip_002.png/250px-Google_Sycamore_Chip_002.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Google_Sycamore_Chip_002.png)

Google Sycamore quantum computer processor in 2019

28 August – Quantum engineers working for Google report the largest chemical simulation on a [quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computer "Quantum computer") – a [Hartree–Fock approximation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartree%E2%80%93Fock_method "Hartree–Fock method") with a [Sycamore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sycamore_(quantum_computer) "Sycamore (quantum computer)") computer paired with a classical computer that analyzed results to provide new parameters for a 12-qubit system.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-333)[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-334)[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-335)
*   2 September – Researchers present an eight-user city-scale [quantum communication network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_network "Quantum network"), located in [Bristol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bristol "Bristol"), England, using already deployed fibres without active switching or trusted nodes.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-336)[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-337)
*   9 September – [Xanadu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xanadu_Quantum_Technologies "Xanadu Quantum Technologies") offers a cloud quantum computing service, using a photonic quantum computer.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-338)
*   21 September – Researchers report the achievement of quantum entanglement between the [motion of a millimetre-sized mechanical oscillator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vibrations_of_a_circular_membrane "Vibrations of a circular membrane") and a disparate distant spin system of a cloud of atoms.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-339)[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-340)
*   3 December – Chinese researchers claim to have achieved [quantum supremacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_supremacy "Quantum supremacy"), using a [photonic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_optical_quantum_computing "Linear optical quantum computing") peak 76-qubit system (43 average) known as _[Jiuzhang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiuzhang\_(quantum\_computer) "Jiuzhang (quantum computer)")_, which performed calculations at 100 trillion times the speed of classical supercomputers.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-341)[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-342)[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-343)
*   29 October – Honeywell introduces a subscription for a quantum computing service, known as quantum computing as a service, with an ion trap quantum computer.[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-344)
*   12 December – At the IEEE International Electron Devices Meeting (IEDM), IMEC shows an RF multiplexer chip that operates at temperatures as low as a few millikelvins, designed for quantum computers. Researchers from the Chalmers University of Technology report the development of a cryogenic low-noise amplifier (LNA) for amplifying signals from qubits, made of indium phosphide (InP) high-electron-mobility transistors (HEMTs).[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-345)
*   21 December – Publication of research of "[counterfactual quantum communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interaction-free_measurement "Interaction-free measurement")" – whose first achievement was reported in 2017 – by which information can be exchanged without any physical particle traveling between observers and without quantum teleportation.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-346) The research suggests that this is based on some form of relation between the properties of modular angular momentum.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-347)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-348)[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-349)

*   6 January – Chinese researchers report that they have built the world's largest integrated quantum communication network, combining over 700 optical fibers with two [QKD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_key_distribution "Quantum key distribution")-ground-to-satellite links for a total distance between nodes of the network of up to ~4,600 km.[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-350)[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-351)
*   13 January – Austrian researchers report the first realization of an [entangling gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_NOT_gate "Controlled NOT gate") between two [logical qubits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_error_correction "Quantum error correction") encoded in [topological quantum error-correction codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toric_code "Toric code") using a [trapped-ion quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trapped_ion_quantum_computer "Trapped ion quantum computer") with 10 ions.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-352)[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-353)
*   15 January – Researchers in China report the successful transmission of entangled photons between [drones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drone_(aircraft) "Drone (aircraft)"), used as nodes for the development of mobile quantum networks or flexible network extensions, marking the first work in which entangled particles were sent between two moving devices.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-354)[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-355)
*   27 January – [BMW](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BMW "BMW") announces the use of a quantum computer for the optimization of supply chains.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-356)
*   28 January – Swiss and German researchers report the development of a highly efficient single-photon source for quantum information technology with a system of gated quantum dots in a tunable microcavity which captures photons released from excited "artificial atoms".[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-357)[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-358)
*   3 February – Microsoft starts offering a cloud quantum computing service, called [Azure Quantum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Azure_Quantum "Microsoft Azure Quantum").[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-359)
*   5 February – Researchers demonstrate a first prototype of quantum-logic gates for [distributed quantum computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_network#Quantum_networks_for_computation "Quantum network").[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-360)[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-361)
*   11 March – Honeywell announces a quantum computer with a quantum volume of 512.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-362)
*   13 April – In a [preprint](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preprint "Preprint"), an astronomer describes for the first time how one could search for quantum communication [transmissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information_science "Quantum information science") sent by [extraterrestrial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterrestrial_intelligence "Extraterrestrial intelligence") using existing telescope and receiver technology. He also provides arguments for why future searches of [SETI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_for_Extraterrestrial_Intelligence "Search for Extraterrestrial Intelligence") should also target interstellar quantum communications.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-363)[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-364)
*   7 May – Two studies complement research published September 2020 by [quantum-entangling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement#Entanglement_of_macroscopic_objects "Quantum entanglement") two mechanical oscillators.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-365)[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-366)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-367)
*   8 June – Researchers from [Toshiba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toshiba "Toshiba") achieve [quantum communications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_communications "Quantum communications") over optical fibres exceeding 600 km in length, a world-record distance.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-368)[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-369)[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-370)

[![Image 7](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Simplified_scale_model_of_the_quantum_computing_demonstrator_housed_in_two_19-inch_racks_with_major_components_labeled.png/500px-Simplified_scale_model_of_the_quantum_computing_demonstrator_housed_in_two_19-inch_racks_with_major_components_labeled.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Simplified_scale_model_of_the_quantum_computing_demonstrator_housed_in_two_19-inch_racks_with_major_components_labeled.png)

Simplified scale mode of a quantum computing demonstrator housed in two 19-inch racks with major components labeled

*   17 June – Austrian, German and Swiss researchers present a quantum computing demonstrator fitting into two standard 19-inch [racks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_rack "Server rack"), the world's first quality standards-meeting compact quantum computer.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-371)[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-10.1103/PRXQuantum.2.020343-372)
*   29 June – IBM demonstrates [quantum advantage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_supremacy "Quantum supremacy").[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-373)
*   1 July – [Rigetti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigetti_Computing "Rigetti Computing") develops a method to join several quantum processor chips together.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-374)
*   7 July – American researchers present a programmable [quantum simulator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_simulator "Quantum simulator") that can operate with 256 qubits,[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-375)[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-376) and on the same date and journal another team presents a quantum simulator of 196 [Rydeberg atoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rydberg_atom "Rydberg atom") trapped in [optical tweezers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_tweezer "Optical tweezer").[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-377)
*   25 October – Chinese researchers report that they have developed the world's fastest programmable quantum computers. The photon-based _Jiuzhang 2_ is claimed to calculate a task in one millisecond, that otherwise would have taken a conventional computer 30 trillion years to complete. Additionally, _Zuchongzhi 2_ is a 66-qubit programmable superconducting quantum computer that was claimed to be the world's fastest quantum computer that can run a calculation task one million times more complex than Google's [Sycamore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sycamore_processor "Sycamore processor"), as well as being 10 million times faster.[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-378)[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-379)
*   11 November – The first simulation of [baryons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baryon "Baryon") on a quantum computer is reported by [University of Waterloo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Waterloo "University of Waterloo"), Canada.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-380)[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-381)
*   16 November – IBM claims that it has created a 127-quantum bit processor, '[IBM Eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Eagle "IBM Eagle")', which according to a report is the most powerful quantum processor known. According to the report, the company had not yet published an academic paper describing its metrics, performance or abilities.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-382)[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-383)

*   18 January – Europe's first quantum annealer with more than 5,000 qubits is presented in Jülich, Germany.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-384)
*   24 March – The first prototype, photonic, quantum [memristive device](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memristor "Memristor"), for [neuromorphic (quantum-) computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuromorphic_computing "Neuromorphic computing") and [artificial neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network "Artificial neural network"), that is "able to produce memristive dynamics on single-photon states through a scheme of measurement and classical feedback" is invented.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-385)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-386)
*   29 March - Researchers at Intel and [Delft University of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delft_University_of_Technology "Delft University of Technology") publish data on the first qubits fabricated on 300 mm wafers in a semiconductor manufacturing facility using all-optical lithography and fully industrial processing.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-387)
*   14 April – The [Quantinuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantinuum "Quantinuum") System Model H1-2 doubles its performance claiming to be the first commercial quantum computer to pass [quantum volume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_volume "Quantum volume") 4096.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-388)
*   26 May – A universal set of computational operations on fault-tolerant quantum bits is demonstrated by a team of experimental physicists in Innsbruck, Austria.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-389)
*   22 June – The world's first quantum computer [integrated circuit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_circuit "Integrated circuit") is demonstrated.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-390)[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-391)
*   28 June – Physicists report that [interstellar quantum communication by other civilizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence#Quantum_communications "Search for extraterrestrial intelligence") could be possible and may be advantageous, identifying some potential challenges and factors for detecting such. They may use, for example, X-ray photons for remotely established [quantum communications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_communication "Quantum communication") and quantum teleportation as the communication mode.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-392)[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-393)
*   21 July – A universal [qudit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qubit#Qudits_and_qutrits "Qubit") quantum processor is demonstrated with trapped ions.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-394)
*   15 August – _[Nature Materials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature\_Materials "Nature Materials")_ publishes the first work showing optical initialization and coherent control of nuclear spin qubits in 2D materials (an ultrathin hexagonal [boron nitride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boron_nitride "Boron nitride")).[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-395)
*   24 August – _[Nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature\_(journal) "Nature (journal)")_ publishes the first research related to a set of 14 photons entangled with high efficiency and in a defined way.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-396)
*   26 August – Created photon pairs at several different frequencies using optical ultra-thin resonant [metasurfaces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_metasurface "Electromagnetic metasurface") made up of arrays of [nanoresonators](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sanomechanical_resonator&action=edit&redlink=1 "Sanomechanical resonator (page does not exist)") is reported.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-397)
*   29 August – Physicists at the [Max Planck Institute for Quantum Optics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Quantum_Optics "Max Planck Institute of Quantum Optics") deterministically generate entangled [graph states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_state "Graph state") of up to 14 photons using a trapped rubidium atom in an optical cavity.[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-398)
*   2 September – Researchers from The University of Tokyo and other Japanese institutions develop a systematic method that applies optimal control theory (GRAPE algorithm) to identify the theoretically optimal sequence from among all conceivable quantum operation sequences. It is necessary to complete the operations within the time that the coherent quantum state is maintained.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-399)
*   30 September – Researchers at University of New South Wales, Australia, achieve a coherence time of two milliseconds, 100 times higher than the previous benchmark in the same quantum processor.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-400)
*   9 November – IBM presents its 433-qubit 'Osprey' quantum processor, the successor to its Eagle system.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-401)[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-402)
*   1 December – The world's first portable quantum computer enters into commerce in [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "Japan"). With three variants, topping out at 3 qubits, they are meant for education. They are based on nuclear magnetic resonance (NMR), "NMR has extremely limited scaling capabilities" and [dimethylphosphite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimethylphosphite "Dimethylphosphite").[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-403)[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-404)[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-405)

*   3 February – At the University of Innsbruck, researchers entangle two ions over a distance of 230 meters.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-406)
*   8 February – [Alpine Quantum Technologies](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alpine_Quantum_Technologies&action=edit&redlink=1 "Alpine Quantum Technologies (page does not exist)") (AQT) demonstrates a [quantum volume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_volume "Quantum volume") of 128 on its 19-inch rack-compatible quantum computer system PINE – a new record in Europe.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-407)
*   17 February – Fusion-based quantum computation is proposed.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-408)
*   27 March – India's first quantum computing-based telecom network link is inaugurated.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-409)
*   14 June – IBM computer scientists report that a quantum computer produced better results for a [physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics "Physics") problem than a conventional [supercomputer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercomputer "Supercomputer").[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-NYT-20230614-410)[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-NAT-20230614-411)
*   21 June – [Microsoft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft") declares that it is working on a [topological quantum computer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topological_quantum_computer "Topological quantum computer") based on [Majorana fermions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majorana_fermion "Majorana fermion"), with the aim of arriving within 10 years at a computer capable of carrying out at least one million operations per second with an error rate of one operation every 1,000 billion (corresponding to 11 uninterrupted days of calculation).[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-412)
*   13 October – Researchers at [TU Darmstadt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt "Technische Universität Darmstadt") publish the first experimental demonstration of a qubit array with more than 1,000 qubits:[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-413)[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-414) A 3,000-site atomic array based on a 2D configuration of optical tweezers[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-link.aps.org-69) holds up to 1,305 atomic qubits.
*   24 October – [Atom Computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom_Computing "Atom Computing") announces that it has "created a 1,225-site atomic array, currently populated with 1,180 qubits",[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-415) based on [Rydberg atoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rydberg_atom "Rydberg atom").[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-416)
*   4 December – IBM presents its 1121-qubit '[Condor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Condor "IBM Condor")' quantum processor, the successor to its [Osprey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Osprey "IBM Osprey") and [Eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Eagle "IBM Eagle") systems.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-417)[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-418) The Condor system was the culmination of IBM's multi-year 'Roadmap to Quantum Advantage' seeking to break the 1,000 qubit threshold.[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-419)
*   6 December – A group led by Misha Lukin at Harvard University realises a programmable quantum processor based on logical qubits using reconfigurable neutral atom arrays.[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-420)

*   14 February – Researchers at [UNSW Sydney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNSW_Sydney "UNSW Sydney") demonstrated control[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-421) of [antimony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antimony "Antimony")-based materials, including [antimonides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antimonides "Antimonides"), in quantum computing. These materials enable high-dimensional [Schrödinger-cat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_cat "Schrödinger cat")[quantum states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_state "Quantum state") ([qudits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qudit "Qudit")), with enhanced scalability and error resilience, utilizing the nucleus [spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_spin "Nuclear spin") of [123Sb antimony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isotopes_of_antimony "Isotopes of antimony") embedded in [silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon "Silicon")[nanoelectronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanoelectronics "Nanoelectronics").[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-422)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-423)
*   21 February – [UCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_College_London "University College London") researchers achieved 97% precision in placing single [arsenic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arsenic "Arsenic") atoms in silicon lattices using [scanning tunneling microscopy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scanning_tunneling_microscopy "Scanning tunneling microscopy"), enabling scalable, low-error qubit arrays for quantum computing.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-424)
*   25 February – Researchers at the [California Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology "California Institute of Technology") demonstrated multiplexed entanglement generation in quantum network nodes, entangling remote quantum memories using multiple distinct emitters. By embedding [ytterbium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ytterbium "Ytterbium") atoms in [yttrium orthovanadate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yttrium_orthovanadate "Yttrium orthovanadate") (YVO 4) crystals and coupling them to optical cavities, they enabled parallel transmission of entangled photons, scaling the entanglement rate with the number of qubits.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-425)
*   12 March – Physicists at [EPFL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPFL "EPFL") directly observed dissipative phase transitions (DPTs) in a superconducting [Kerr resonator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerr_frequency_comb "Kerr frequency comb"). Their experiment confirmed both first- and second-order DPTs, revealing critical slowing down and metastability effects, which could lead to more stable quantum computing and ultra-sensitive quantum sensors.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-426)
*   1 May – Researchers at Intel show data using a cryogenic 300-mm wafer prober to collect high-volume data on hundreds of industry-manufactured spin qubit devices at 1.6 K. Devices were characterized in the single electrons across full wafers with high yield.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-427)
*   8 May – Researchers deterministically fuse small quantum states into states with up to eight qubits.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-428)
*   10 May – Researchers from Google and the [Paul Scherrer Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Scherrer_Institute "Paul Scherrer Institute") developed a new hybrid digital-analog quantum simulator, combining the strengths of both techniques. This innovation enhanced the precision and flexibility of quantum computing while enabling more accurate modeling of complex quantum processes.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-429)[[e]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-430)
*   30 May – Researchers at Photonic and Microsoft perform a teleported CNOT gate between qubits physically separated by 40 meters, confirming remote quantum entanglement between T-centers.[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-431)
*   30 June – Researchers from [Oxford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University "Oxford University") successfully linked two quantum processors via an optical fiber network, enabling distributed quantum computing by demonstrating quantum entanglement between distant qubits, paving the way for scalable modular quantum computers and the development of a quantum internet.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-432)
*   5 August – Research from [Brown University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_University "Brown University") discovered fractional [excitons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excitons "Excitons") in bilayer [graphene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphene "Graphene") under the fractional quantum [Hall effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hall_effect "Hall effect"), expanding excitonic understanding and quantum computing potential.[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-433)
*   26 August – Researchers at [Northwestern University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwestern_University "Northwestern University") successfully teleported a quantum state of light over 30 kilometres (19 mi) of fiber optic cable carrying conventional internet traffic, demonstrating the feasibility of integrating quantum communication into existing networks.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-434)
*   29 August – Researchers at [Empa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empa "Empa") successfully constructed a one-dimensional alternating [Heisenberg model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_Heisenberg_model "Quantum Heisenberg model") using synthetic nanographenes, confirming century-old quantum physics predictions. Their work marked a significant step toward real-world quantum technologies such as ultra-fast computing and unbreakable encryption.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-435)
*   2 December – Physicists observed quantum entanglement within individual [protons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protons "Protons"), demonstrating that entanglement, a key concept in quantum computing, extended to the subatomic level, revealing the complex interdependence of [quarks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quarks "Quarks") and [gluons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gluons "Gluons") within protons.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-436)
*   9 December – Google Quantum AI announced [Willow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willow_processor "Willow processor"), the first quantum processor where error-corrected qubits get exponentially better as they get bigger. Willow performed a standard benchmark computation in under five minutes that would take today's fastest supercomputers 10 septillion years.[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-437)[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-438)
*   15 December – Researchers at [Oak Ridge National Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oak_Ridge_National_Laboratory "Oak Ridge National Laboratory") in collaboration with [EPB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPB "EPB") and the [University of Tennessee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Tennessee "University of Tennessee") achieved transmission of entangled quantum signals with 100% uptime through a commercial fiber-optic network for over 30 hours using automatic polarization compensation to prevent disruptions from environmental factors.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-439)[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-440)[[f]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-441)
*   25 December – Researchers at Intel demonstrate a test chip with 12 spin-qubits fabricated using immersion and extreme ultraviolet lithography (EUV), along with other standard high-volume manufacturing (HVM) processes.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-442) This doubles the number of spin qubits published in September 2022.[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-443)

*   7 January – Researchers at [Osaka Metropolitan University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osaka_Metropolitan_University "Osaka Metropolitan University") derived a simplified formula for quantum entanglement entropy, allowing for easier analysis of entanglement in strongly correlated electron systems. Their study identified unexpected quantum behaviors in nanoscale artificial magnetic materials and highlighted the role of quantum relative entropy in the [Kondo effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kondo_effect "Kondo effect").[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-444)
*   14 February – Researchers (Björkman _et al._) used [transmon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transmon "Transmon") qubits to demonstrate a [virtual-state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_state "Virtual state") process of the [Landau-Zener](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landau%E2%80%93Zener_transition "Landau–Zener transition")-Stückelberg-Majorana (LZSM) transition.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Bj%C3%B6rkman-445)[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-446)[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-447)[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-448) Their experiment significantly suppressed the AC [Stark shift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stark_effect#Problems "Stark effect"), improving control over quantum state transitions.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Bj%C3%B6rkman-445)[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-449)
*   19 February – Microsoft announced [Majorana 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majorana_1 "Majorana 1"), the first quantum processing unit based on a topological core.[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Forbes_Majorana-450) The research created a new class of materials called [topoconductors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topoconductor "Topoconductor"), which use topological superconductivity to control hardware-protected topological qubits and determined fermion parity in Majorana zero modes.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-BBC_Majorana_1-451)[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-InAs_Single_Shot-452)
*   27 February – [Amazon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_(company) "Amazon (company)") announced[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-453) a quantum computing processor prototype, nicknamed "Ocelot", that utilizes cat qubits for bosonic quantum error correction.[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-454)
*   26 March – Researchers at [JPMorganChase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase "JPMorgan Chase") and [Quantinuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantinuum "Quantinuum") announced the realization of [certified randomness](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Certified_randomness&action=edit&redlink=1 "Certified randomness (page does not exist)"), generating publicly certifiable bits using a trapped-ion quantum processor.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-455)[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-456)

*   [List of companies involved in quantum computing or communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_companies_involved_in_quantum_computing_or_communication "List of companies involved in quantum computing or communication")

Bennett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_H._Bennett_(physicist) "Charles H. Bennett (physicist)") (2021) citing Bennett CH, Bessette F, [Brassard G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilles_Brassard "Gilles Brassard"), Salvail L, [Smolin J](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_A._Smolin "John A. Smolin") (1992) "[Experimental quantum cryptography.](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/BF00191318)" [J Cryptol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journal_of_Cryptology "Journal of Cryptology") 5(1): 3–28. In Bennett, Bessette _et al_. (1992) the year of "manuscript written" by Wiesner is "_circa_ 1970".[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-5)
2.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_ref-18)**Some sources state that: an idea in Park's paper was used as[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-MrBSaam-10) information for what was later undertood by proof as the [no-cloning theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No-cloning_theorem "No-cloning theorem") circa 1982.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Bertlmann&Friis-9)[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-MrBSaam-10) An alternative position is: the no-cloning theorem was discovered in 1982 without mentioning 1969/1970.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-11)[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-12) Sources state Park proved mathematically no-cloning explicitly as a reality[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-13)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-14) though his paper makes no mention explicitly of the term as it is now known.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-Park-8)[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-15) An alternative position: simply, Park 1970 was the origin of the no-cloning theorem without mentioning 1982.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-16) One further position states Park was first to show the existence of no-cloning - this quantum mechanical reality was rediscovered in 1982 and 2013.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-17)
3.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_ref-20)**Holevo's paper is the first published on the subject of [quantum information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information "Quantum information") according to the [Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_Encyclopedia_of_Philosophy "Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy") (Michael Cuffaro)[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_note-19)
4.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_quantum_computing_and_communication#cite_ref-31)**Submission received by the [IJoTP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Journal_of_Theoretical_Physics "International Journal of Theoretical Physics"): May 7, 1981
